< review>
Another fake Italian restaurant or pizzeria as you would like to call. We are from Italy, in vacation in this beautiful city, with a young daughter that is not confident with spicy American /Mexican food that is generally served with tons of sauces and other stuff like that. For this reason we chosen this place according with the reviews. I would to point out that the waiter was quite gentle and nice,, so for this a honor mention. On the food, we had pizza and salads.. Better no add any comments. I'm pretty sure that majority of Americans that never tried the real original Italian pizza, this could be good. So, if I were an American, probably I would have been aligned with the majority of the comments, unfortunately I'm Italian, so my comments is mainly for my fellows: if you are in the city and you want to eat a pizza.. Pls wait to come to home. Two stars only for the kindness of the waiters.<//review>

< Review>
Best thin crust pizza in Marin!  I love this place.  The food is good, down home Italian cooking.  Nothing fancy and all dressed up so that it looks like Italian, tastes like cardboard, and you pay way too much for it.  It's real food made by real people who want you to have a good meal.  It feels like you're sitting in their living room.  Small, cozy, and family feeling.  Everyone who works here is genuinely interested in you having an excellent dining experience.

If you're lucky, you'll go on a  night when one of the guys makes these awesome little powered sugar donuts.  YUM!!!

My hubby always gets the calzone or pasta.  I'm a chicken parm or a chicken piccata girl, myself.  Our kid always gets the bambino pizza (or we get a small and have it as our appetizer leaving him to fight for the last couple pieces for his dinner!)  The bread fresh from the oven is to die for but always fills me up way too much before dinner.  This last time, the waitress brought bread that we couldn't finish so we took it home for a yummy late night snack :)

We have never had a bad meal.  In fact, this is our go-to place for Italian.  My only wish is that they were open 24 hours.  But we love the couple that owns the place, so I guess they deserve a little time off.

Eccellente, Napoli!  Eccellente!</Review>

The best traditional Vietnamese rice plate with grilled pork in the Bay Area. They also have good Pho. If you have friends wanted to check out Vietnamese food, bring them here.</review>
<rate>5< /rate><Pics>None<//Pics><user_name>Chloe Nguyen</user_name><Date>1476294859727</Date><GmapID>0x808fcd2aefb35ccd:0x5a00bdf1d69dc456< /GmapID></record></dataset><record>
<Response>None</Response>< text>
In A Nutshell:

-If you can find parking in the small parking lot, then Com Tam Thien Huong is worth it.
-The interior design is nice, feels upscale.
-They serve other dishes like pho, hu tieu & bun, but they are well-known for their com tam.
-Com tam is "broken rice", which is supposed to be the broken pieces of rice at the bottom of the rice bag that the poor people would end up eating.
-Thankfully, Vietnamese are some of the most clever & best cooks in the world so they definitely make due w/ any ingredient they have at their disposal.
-The com tam served here is very good, nice presentation w/ thinly sliced bbq pork chops.

Overall, if you can find parking then this is a great place to grab some com tam in Little Saigon - San Jose.< /text>

almost $8,000.000 later, after literally paying to have EVERYTHING replaced in the suspension, exhaust, and drivetrain on a chevy van project, I am still having issues. especially in my rear end....

Very poor workmanship...

I had brought in a van project to be restored  about a year ago now.
At first I had my front shocks and control arms done, along with my brakes, Which the seemed to do a great job with.

Since then, it seemed like EVERY TIME I had more work done, more and more extra parts and labor charges kept accumulating IN THE MIDDLE OF THE JOB.

I had brought in my own parts, but it seems like every time, other things needed ordered or replaced.

I am a rather proficient mechanic myself, but have no lift or garage, nor the time to work on such a large project.  When i first received my vehicle back after a motor swap, the vehicle knock sensor was installed on the top of the block, instead of by the starter on the bottom, and the timing was done completely backwards, and my vacuum lines where hooked up backwards as well. (MY MOTOR WAS ACTUALLY SUCKING CHARCOAL FROM THE CANISTER INSTEAD OF BEING LET OUT FROM THE THROTTLE BODY) it had kept tripping codes, NAMELY the kncok sensor, and speed sensor (which was do to rough idle from non existent vacuum in the system) and instead of checking over the motor to make sure it was hooked up[ right, they decided to change my speed sensor (i had already had a new transmission installed at this point, so 600.00 labor and parts for a brand new sensor being replaced again....

If you want the Cadillac experience of camping, rafting and eating you need to visit these guys.

I consistently bring large groups to them, and this past weekend brought 50 folks. They had tents built with sleeping pads in them waiting when we came, served incredible meals like eggs, potatoes and toast and fruit for breakfast, and amazing steak, chicken and veggie dinner and awesome sandwiches for lunch. They don't skimp on anything!!! The customer experience is always top of mind.

And the raft guides... oh the raft guides! They are best in class, super safe, super funny, and  a joy to work with--tip them well, they will appreciate it so much!

The campgrounds are just gorgeous! You're nestled in these little private areas that are riverfront and the amenities are great! On one side of camp they have warm running water bathrooms with showers, and a changing room and on the other side they have portable toilets for folks who don't want to walk far at night.

If you have the chance to go rafting, do it with Adventure Connection! They do wine tasting, rafting, group deals if you bring a large enough group and a customer experience that is second to none. Love these guys!</Text>< Response>

<review>AC/Mariah is a well organized and fun rafting and camping company.  We were there for a full day of rafting on the South Fork of the American River.  Unlike other companies I've rafted with, these guys offer wetsuits and helmets in addition to the requisite life jackets.  We lucked out with perfect, hot weather so even though the snow melt water was cold, most of us enjoyed plunging into the water to cool off.  It was a very crowded day on the river but these guys kept our group of 3 rafts close together.  The hearty, tasty lunch was held at their campground half way through the 21 mile trip.  Also, unlike my other experiences, this company had showers and changing rooms for us to use at the end of the day.  All in all a great company and exciting trip down the river.<//review>< Pictures>

<Review>written: 1/31/13

ONE DAY OF WONDERFUL

We had a wonderful day on our one-day trip down the American River - South Fork, last summer. We booked through Travel Zoo and I'm trying to decide if I'd like to buy another one of their great deals for this year, while it's on sale.

It was easy to book the trip once we'd purchased the deal. It was harder for us to figure out a weekend my husband would be home, that we were both free. We ended up going close to the end of summer and it was beautiful weather.

There was a good-sized group of people and it was easy to find the meeting location. Lunch was served half-way through the day and it was pretty good.  The guides were friendly and had a lot of experience so I never felt unsafe.  My husband jumped out of the raft in one rapids are where they said the brave could safely navigate craft-free. I am not the brave. He survived though.

The two-day package sounds like a lot of fun, but it'd be too much for me. One day was plenty! We brought our Fuji camera (waterproof) and got some great shots! We also bought a professional one. There were two companies selling them with comparable prices. We just picked the shot we liked best and went with it.

The current special offered through TravelZoo is $79 for the one-day trip with lunch (regularly $160). I believe we paid $80 each last year, also.</Review><GmapID>0x809aff9b6b15bec3:0xfd2d5fef704ef01</GmapID>< date>

<Text>Over the past 25 years I have taken at least 15 rafting trips down the South Fork of The American River. It was great fun and we all joked and bantered back and forth and the raft guide also joined in on the fun. <rate>5< /rate><Text>Reservations/Bookings:
Such a great company with great service and flexibility. I ended up in a pickle, had bought the North Fork trip for 2 people (on a weekday, lunch included) and booked the trip in April 2015. I also reserved and paid for the wetsuits that were required since I did not own any. Received a call back that the trip had to be cancelled because the water levels were just not high enough due to the drought. AC refunded the amount I paid for the wetsuits and said I could switch to either a South Fork or Middle Fork trip (either weekday or weekend since weekdays are cheaper than weekends) and lunch included at no extra cost.

I did not book right the trip right away since I had to check with my friend about the dates available to go. Called Adventure Connection and left a message. About 30 minutes after, I received a call from Nathan Rangel (President of Adventure Connection). He was superb in every way about handling the reservation details and was very informative, answered all my questions. I had to email him the voucher codes and he was also very prompt, booked my trip and emailed me the same day with all the forms to fill out along with trip preparation guidelines, etc. Overall, just a great company with how they handled cancelled trips, re-booking, and customer service. I recommend AC to my friends and family, and everyone I meet that are looking forward to an awesome whitewater experience.

The Trip:
I feel so bad I forgot our guide's name since it has been awhile, however he was great in that he was very confident in his skills and was knowledgeable about the surrounding areas and spots to go to if you wanted to do things other than whitewater rafting. He was from Montana and grew up rafting so I felt very safe with him being our guide. We even stopped to pick blackberries off the vines for a bit, which was nice. During a maneuver, our raft rammed into a rock head first. I sat in the back left and was totally knocked out of the raft and could have ended up in an eddy on the side, but he was very quick and by the time I knew it, I was getting pulled back onto the raft. He was so awesome! You will be safe with AC and their guides!</Text>< Pictures>

< text>
This is for the experience in May 2013.

Wonderful experience! The BF's boss organized this trip for a bunch of their co-workers and I took the day off to join~ I am so glad I did.

We were running a tad late, but they were very friendly and told us not to worry. Our party was big enough to fill two rafts and it was a Friday during early season.

We were greeted by Jeffrey who kindly collected all our waivers and loaded us up with gear! I must warn you if you are a germaphobe bring your own life jacket since it does smell a bit. But you will get used to the smell because you will just keep getting wet!  Gear = helmet (mainly to protect your heads from bumping too hard), life jacket and paddle!

Then on to the bus we went~ got dropped off at the location. We separated into two groups I was on the raft with Riley leading us. He was awesome!!! We quickly went through some practice paddling and off we went!

Class III rapids come after lunch~

LUNCH WAS GREAT! I checked Yelp to see how the lunch was, since some of these types of trips do not provide enough and the BF gets hungry~ wanted to be prepared! But that was not a concern! No skimping out there! We can even get seconds. I don't know what it was but I thought the burgers were delicious... not sure why people were raving about cookies. They do veggie burgers as well (you might need to request it)

Riley had us ride a wave and did it three times, told us about the funny shaped rocks (gorilla shaped, Ronald Reagan shaped --- I think it looks more like Elivis, etc) and was just an all around chill and happy guide!

BRING CASH! So you can tip them! They deserve it~ they spend the whole day with you and they use your name as much as possible...haha dedication!< /text>

< text>
Family owned donut shop. They're very nice and quick getting through the line if there is one. The raised donuts are very big and fluffy. I like to get the apple fritter, but if I'm not early enough, they're sold out. The bear claws have apple filling. They can also fill bars with creme if you ask for it. I've picked up mixed dozens for work several times and they're always a hit. They have a good variety of raised, cake, old fashioned, etc. They used to be cash only but they accept cards now. Parking lot is good sized for the shopping center.</text>

This is a really good donut shop.  I love lemon filled and they have it at Vasy's.  I find most donut shops don't.  You can tell high quality  ingredients are used to make the donuts.  There was another place I went to in Fremont that had great donuts too and  is much closer to where I live (near Newpark Mall) but they changed owners and it isn't nearly as good anymore...  i went there for over 25 yrs.  Now I drive to Vasy's  (after a recommendation)  it is a few miles further but worth the drive.  The help is also very nice. <Rate>5< /Rate>< name>
Marissa Lawrence</name>
< gmap_id>
0x80c2b8c7531a48eb:0x83f1c1c6066078d5</gmap_id>
<Date>1548484431932</Date><Pictures>None< /Pictures>< userid>
111603940148989488500< /userid>
<response>None< /response>< Review>
A terrific, old-school bookstore in a ritzy part of LA (Larchmont in Hancock Park). This is an old part of town with a neighborly feel and Chevalier is part of this small community which hardly feels like LA (at least not to a Westsider).

Not far from the mansions once occupied mainly by WASPs (the sort who sent their girls to Marlborough rather than Westlake, and not just because of proximity), it's far more heterogeneously upscale now. The Greek restaurant across the street is well-regarded but the service was so bad that Mom and I left. Also there was an obnoxious, loud talker next to us and there was no way we could deal with her incessant nasal chatter for an hour.

The children's section is terrific and the people who work there love books, even the kids. I was there for a private reading of Joe Domanick's Blue, his second book about the LAPD.

In the age of Kindle, Chevalier's is a throwback to a more literate age. Brentano's and Dutton's in Brentwood closed long ago. Our Village Bookstore in the Palisades closed a couple years ago.

But Chevalier's is going strong. If it didn't take 90 f****** minutes to get there from WLA at 4PM, I might go back just to browse. Hancock Park is one of THE worst parts of Los Angeles to get to if you're in WLA. There's just no good way: if you take the 10, you're too far South. If you take surface streets, well, it takes forever.

But Hancock Park is a great neighborhood for people who work downtown or in mid-Wilshire. It's just a nonstarter for Westsiders unless you go in the middle of the day or on a weekend.< /Review>

<Name>Charle Kennedy< /Name><date>1621365973950</date><Rating>4< /Rating>< text>
Pros: Great location in Westwood, which is NOT Beverly Hills, but a 5-minute drive so very close! Guestrooms are functional and include a small lounge chair + ottoman set, a work space/desk and mini fridge. The lobby and its restrooms are really beautiful, clean, spacious and luxurious. The daily credit to be used at the lobby mini store, which carries plenty of essentials and convenient items, was quite the pleasant surprise. And 9/10 staffers go above and beyond. Note: you can text the front desk with any requests or questions, super convenient!!

Cons: The walls are thin. Paid parking. Pool hours are more like office hours (something like 9am-5pm) and the pool is almost completely covered by shade so it's a bit cold.

Pandemic modifications: What was once paid valet parking is now overpriced self parking for $49/night. I don't mind self parking and I don't mind paid parking, but the cost seems a bit high seeing as you're doing it yourself. There is no room service or housekeeping so if you request new bedding, anticipate that it will be left outside your room in a massive Ziploc-style bag.< /text>

< Review>
So overall this hotel definitely earned its 5-stars. It was very clean and the rooms themselves were immaculate and extremely comfortable. The front desk personnel was also extremely accommodating, we originally asked for a king realized it was bit small for the three of us (me, my mom, and younger sister) and they switched us over, zero questions, to a double.

Now here‚Äôs the part where I warn you of all additional charges that I didn‚Äôt know of when booking through Priceline.
Parking: they have a 47/day parking fee (no valet) it is self-parking.
We opted to park on the street for free but you have to be wary of the posted signs in order to avoid a ticket and/or getting towed.
Hotel fee: they charge 26 a day in hotel fees. BUT you do get to spend 15 of those in their little food pantry area so it‚Äôs more like 11 a day.

COVID 19 changes: restaurant was closed and pool closed early, I believe at 6 so by the time we got back from exploring the city it was closed.

Overall extremely accommodating 2 night stay. Would definitely revisit.<//Review>

<user_id>105719298610009137684< /user_id>< Name>
Julie B< /Name>
< Time>
1570241739801< /Time>
<Rating>4<//Rating>< text>
The staff of the Kimpton Palomar was friendly and accommodating.  The hotel is situated mid block on Wilshire in a neighborhood area. It isn't too far of a walk to the shopping area near UCLA, but otherwise there are no stores nearby. The restaurant on property has delicious avocado toast. The lobby has a lot of seating and various areas to play games or mingle with friends. The property has rental bikes that can be used in the area. The rooms are small, which is pretty typical in the area. The beds are comfortable and showers have good water pressure.  The hotel gym has two poorly situated Peloton bikes which are under a beam so when a rider is doing a ride with arm exercises it is likely that he or she will hit the low ceiling that is above the bikes. When I stayed at the hotel the bikes were not properly calibrated either. So, if you are an avid Peloton Rider be cognizant of your output as you may just hit an unrealistic PR while barely breaking a sweat.</text>

< text>
We are huge fans of Kimpton hotels, and the Palomar is no exception. The rooms are spacious and comfortable, with good amenities and comfy robes. The right amount of luxurious and practical. The lobby is modern and inviting with chic d√©cor, and the pool area is small but private - unlike many of the see-and-be-seen Los Angeles area hotels, I appreciate this practical use of pool area. Room service was great - the food was good, and it came swiftly. The staff was very nice and acted very friendly and human for a change. We had our two small dogs with us, and we appreciate that Kimpton Hotels are dog-friendly. Not just that but dog-friendly, and well-designed. They don't stick us in a smelly gross, dog-designated hotel room, they are truly dog-friendly. I think parking was kind of pricey but that is standard for any hotel in the area. I am happy and satisfied with our decision to have chosen this Kimpton, and would definitely recommend this place to friends and stay here again.< /text>

<Review>I loved the email offer of having a framed photo of my choice waiting for me to make the room feel like home. It wasn't actually in the room when I checked in, but they brought it up within 20 minutes or so after I asked about it - pretty quick on a busy Friday afternoon. The king bed is not the most comfy, but the room is nice and stylish. I did have to call downstairs to have the sink faucet tightened to the sink. It operates by moving one handle left and right, but the actual faucet stand moved too, making it difficult to actually turn it on and off. The pool area is cute and only gets direct sun until about 3:30pm right now. While the sun is there, it is TOASTY. No hot tub or active drink service, but you can get drinks in plastic cups from the bar to bring in yourself. < Review>
The team at the Kimpton Palomar in Beverly Hills go over the top in catering to their guests. The ONLY FAIR comparison I can give this experience is that of being on a cruise ship and having a room steward. YOU LITERALLY PICK UP THE PHONE OR APPROACH A TEAM MEMBER AND ANY REQUEST IS IMMEDIATELY  MET!!!   I have stayed here twice, with approximately one month between trips, each trip for one week at a time.  Both stays were wonderful! The hotel Manager, Noah/Noel (excuse my bad memory) ensures that everyone from management to the valet goes the extra mile to ensure you feel catered to.  I ordered an off-menu request twice for a to-go breakfast, through the front desk, and my order was ready within minutes for me to pick up on my way out the door.  They practically met me at the lobby elevator with my order in hand. I did not get transferred to the restaurant or even told that my off menu request couldn't be accommodated. The front desk and restaurant completely took care of me without hesitation. The restaurant and bar Manager, Nielsen also goes far to impress guests. There is a reception every evening from 5-6pm where complimentary select wines, other beverages and appetizers are served. It is an intimate but social setting where Nielsen ensures everyone is having a good time. The bar staff are great! Brad and Brenda were amazing. In the hotel and restaurant/bar, upon my second arrival, at least 5 people welcomed me back within the first 24 hours I was there. Each day, when I would come in from work, the valet would welcome be back and Nielsen and Noah/Noel were in the lobby to welcome guests back as well. Additionally, very convenient for business travelers, hotel management communicated with me via text to ensure all my needs were being met.  The rooms were roomy, clean, and comfy. There is a great mini bar in the room inclusive of any snack or drink you could desire. I could go on forever about how awesome the team at the hotel and restaurant are! They are amazing and I would stay here again and again.  I travel at least 2-3 times per month and stay at many, many places.  This is one of the best hotel/restaurant teams I have experienced by far!< /Review>

115362898003952244191</user>
< Review>
Stayed at the property for the second time, this time for 3 nights (2 with points and 1 with their cyber Monday pricing). The points were booked for the king skyline view, and the paid night on a regular king. Since I am platinum elite, my paid night was upgraded to the same room type as the reward booking, which was fantastic. The view was indeed wonderful (18th floor, near elevator and ice machine, but was quiet the whole stay).

The service was great and was the first time I was properly acknowledged for my platinum elite status at an ihg property for a longer (more than 1 night) stay. We got a bottle of Merlot with a personalized message regarding Thanksgiving, which was a nice touch.

I also took advantage of some of the extra kimpton specific amenities such as hair straightener (so so useful not having to bring mine around from home) as well as a humidifier (I don't think it worked as they forgot to change the filter).

Their restaurant is also pretty fun, with wine hour at 5p everyday. We got their fries one late night and they were a bit stale though.

Pool is great, even in the colder months (just head down in the late morning or early afternoon to catch the sun).

Gym is a bit small so gets crowded. They have a Peloton bike which was nice!

Located in a great area too, with Bird scooters easily accessible to ride to Westwood. Can't wait to stay here again!<//Review>

< Text>
(Translated by Google) It was a great hotel. I will use it again when I go to Los Angeles.

I stayed for a week on a business trip and used valet parking, but there was no problem with other reviews, and it was comfortable. The staff was very polite and nice.

I used the restaurant several times for dinner. The staff and the food were great. The staff remembered the last time the steak was ordered for the second time and was impressed with the hospitality, including the other fine service. Hamburgers and steaks are very delicious and I want to revisit to eat them.

The lobby is stylish and has a fireplace. The room was clean without any problems.

It is convenient because you can easily reach both Santa Monica and Beverly Hills by car.

It's a good hotel that you want to stay in Los Angeles!

< Text>
Nice and affordable hotel in west LA - clearly popular to Scandinavian family travelers. No breakfast included but very good gym and complimentary coffee in the morning. Fairly close to the airport and less than 2km from the UCLA campus. The Hammer museum is 500m away and is a hub for public transportation. We managed to get around LA without a car using hop-on-hop sightseeing bus + Santa Monica or Metro bus to Santa Monica and Venice beaches (all from Hammer), and Uber of course. Make sure you have the Uber app loaded while in LA!</Text>
